  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_37c9a585-6cf0-4a29-909f-c829dd6fe138'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer795162393091910937"><b>"Corpus Bones! I utterly loathe my life."</b><p>Catherine feels trapped. Her father is determined to marry her off to a rich man--any rich man, no matter how awful. </p><p>But by wit, trickery, and luck, Catherine manages to send several would-be husbands packing.   <span id="freeText795162393091910937" style="display:none"><b>"Corpus Bones! I utterly loathe my life."</b><p>Catherine feels trapped. Her father is determined to marry her off to a rich man--any rich man, no matter how awful. </p><p>But by wit, trickery, and luck, Catherine manages to send several would-be husbands packing. Then a shaggy-bearded suitor from the north comes to call--by far the oldest, ugliest, most revolting suitor of them all. </p><p> Unfortunately, he is also the richest. </p><p> Can a sharp-tongued, high-spirited, clever young maiden with a mind of her own actually lose the battle against an ill-mannered, piglike lord and an unimaginative, greedy toad of a father? </p><p> Deus! Not if Catherine has anything to say about it!</p></span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/62079987-melissa"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1546456123i/62079987._UY100_CR24,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/62079987-melissa">Melissa</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I was reluctant to read the book at first because of the title and the cover. I was much more interested in the author's other book The Midwife's Appr<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I was reluctant to read the book at first because of the title and the cover. I was much more interested in the author's other book The Midwife's Apprentice. However, having read both, I just loved this book. I actual ended up rereading it several times over the years. Catherine is not your typical girl and her humor towards her everyday world is often times laugh out loud funny. It is also poignant at times however, and there is a lot of interesting history/customs that can be observed through her diary. I would recommend this book. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_31033828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31033828" />
    <a title="Carre Gardner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1074088-carre-gardner"><img alt="Carre Gardner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444872674p2/1074088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31033828?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carre Gardner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carre Gardner" href="/user/show/1074088-carre-gardner">Carre Gardner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31033828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15376473325839688072">If there were a 6-star rating, I'd give it to this book. When it won the Newbery Medal for Children's Literature, it was Cushman's first book. It's Hi. Lar. I. Ous. Birdy is the 14-year old daughter of a 14th-century landowner in Merrie Olde Englande. While her father plots suitable arranged marriages for her and her mother tries to prepare her for being a wife by teaching her manners, needlework and herbal medicine, Birdy, the ultimate tomboy, plots ways to get rid of the suitors and sneak off </span>
  <span id="freeText15376473325839688072" style="display:none">If there were a 6-star rating, I'd give it to this book. When it won the Newbery Medal for Children's Literature, it was Cushman's first book. It's Hi. Lar. I. Ous. Birdy is the 14-year old daughter of a 14th-century landowner in Merrie Olde Englande. While her father plots suitable arranged marriages for her and her mother tries to prepare her for being a wife by teaching her manners, needlework and herbal medicine, Birdy, the ultimate tomboy, plots ways to get rid of the suitors and sneak off to the village where she can help with the hay harvest and sing hey-nonny-nonny amongst the peasants.<br /><br />The book is written as a journal and spans a year, during which Birdy learns to stop fighting against the position she was born to (including the arranged marriage!) Through her eyes, we come to see and know the village peasants as if they were old friends. It has all the elements relevant to 14-year-old girls in America today: the longing for a best friend; the parent-related angst; the feeling that no one understands you; the compulsion to do something that really matters in the world. Birdy is by turns selfish, generous, compassionate, merciless, moody and serene. It's a brilliant book: one that I read over and over when I need a laugh. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15376473325839688072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

That's the book I want for my kids. You know, if I wasn't half-convinced that I would destroy the poor things with my eccentric brand of madness. <span id="freeTextContainer14349986341976077279">My biggest complaint about this book is how horribly she speaks of her father. We listened to it on CD (edition wasn't available to post) but the girl who does the reading has a very "common" accent. Combined with her sharp tongue I couldn't feel for the character. In fact you are always surprised when she mentions a servant.<br/><br/>It is written in diary format which is so popular for this age group </span>
  <span id="freeText14349986341976077279" style="display:none">My biggest complaint about this book is how horribly she speaks of her father. We listened to it on CD (edition wasn't available to post) but the girl who does the reading has a very "common" accent. Combined with her sharp tongue I couldn't feel for the character. She sounded like she should be cleaning out the stables instead of the daughter of a knight and a lady. In fact you are always surprised when she mentions a servant.<br /><br />It is written in diary format which is so popular for this age group BUT her abrasive personality really makes it so you could care less about her poor plight. (I wonder what I would have thought if I had read it years ago before I had my own daughters...)</span>

<div id="review_135800083" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135800083" />
    <a title="linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19089-linda"><img alt="linda" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135800083?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="linda" href="/user/show/19089-linda">linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19089-linda?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19089-linda?shelf=ya-novels">ya-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer135800083&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135800083" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15048338277892883507">Recently reread this for probably the hundredth time and continue to love Catherine entirely too much. Sadly, a revisit to this book as an adult highlights, to my great despair, that I always wanted her to marry the goatherd, and that part of me has been mourning the fact that she doesn't for like more than a decade. What is my life. Accessible for kids and (obviously) for adults, it felt very in the moment, like I could see and hear and live all the delights and discomforts of Catherine's time </span>
  <span id="freeText15048338277892883507" style="display:none">Recently reread this for probably the hundredth time and continue to love Catherine entirely too much. Sadly, a revisit to this book as an adult highlights, to my great despair, that I always wanted her to marry the goatherd, and that part of me has been mourning the fact that she doesn't for like more than a decade. What is my life. Accessible for kids and (obviously) for adults, it felt very in the moment, like I could see and hear and live all the delights and discomforts of Catherine's time -- still one of the best books I've ever read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15048338277892883507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23102176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12395422980749418972">Cushman's Newbery Honor-winning book is wonderfully evocative, with its remarkably realized, feisty heroine determined to have a say in her own destiny, despite the strictures of her medieval society. Hilarious, endearing, and determined, Birdy's trenchant observations of the life around her are told with a refreshingly earthy honesty so real and direct that you put down the book sadly, feeling like you're being parted from a dear friend. Cushman manages to create her historical period in such i</span>
  <span id="freeText12395422980749418972" style="display:none">Cushman's Newbery Honor-winning book is wonderfully evocative, with its remarkably realized, feisty heroine determined to have a say in her own destiny, despite the strictures of her medieval society. Hilarious, endearing, and determined, Birdy's trenchant observations of the life around her are told with a refreshingly earthy honesty so real and direct that you put down the book sadly, feeling like you're being parted from a dear friend. Cushman manages to create her historical period in such intimate detail that it lives and breathes. This often-challenged book is highly recommended for girls 12 and up who will see themselves in Birdy and be moved and inspired by her story. A must read."<br /><br />CIP: "The thirteen-year-old daughter of an English country knight keeps a journal in which she records the events of her life, particularly her longing for adventure beyond the usual role of women and her efforts to avoid being married off."<br /><br />SLJ: "Grade 6-9. This unusual book provides an insider's look at the life of Birdy, 14, the daughter of a minor English nobleman. The year is 1290 and the vehicle for storytelling is the girl's witty, irreverent diary. She looks with a clear and critical eye upon the world around her, telling of the people she knows and of the daily events in her small manor house... The book is rich with information about the food, dress, religious beliefs, manners, health, medical practices, and sanitary habits (or lack thereof) of the people of her day... A feminist far ahead of her time, she is both believable and lovable... Superb historical fiction."<br /><br />Kirkus: "Unwillingly keeping a journal... Birdy (daughter of a 13th-century knight) makes a terse first entry--``I am bit by fleas and plagued by family. That is all there is to say''--but is soon confiding her pranks and troubles in fascinating detail... The period has rarely been presented for young people with such authenticity; the exotic details will intrigue readers while they relate more closely to Birdy's yen for independence and her sensibilities toward the downtrodden. Her tenacity and ebullient naivete are extraordinary; at once comic and thought-provoking, this first novel is a delight. 12+"</span>
  <a data-text-id="12395422980749418972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_58327724" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58327724" />
    <a title="Heidi-Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/921817-heidi-marie"><img alt="Heidi-Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203556177p2/921817.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/58327724?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi-Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi-Marie" href="/user/show/921817-heidi-marie">Heidi-Marie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=award-winners">award-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=ya-12-19">ya-12-19</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=2009-book-challenge">2009-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/921817-heidi-marie?shelf=tween-10-13">tween-10-13</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58327724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4579347569508646980">This is one of the "classic" books that they like you to read in late elementary school or early junior high. I'm sure it would hold the attention for that age. And it is rather intriguing to read a book set in medieval times, especially with a spunky heroine. But there were quite a few bawdy references, though they were made to be light or humourous. Perhaps it was like that back then, I don't know. I do know that I don't like that kind of humor, or that kind of talk in general. <br/><br/>I certainly did</span>
  <span id="freeText4579347569508646980" style="display:none">This is one of the "classic" books that they like you to read in late elementary school or early junior high. I'm sure it would hold the attention for that age. And it is rather intriguing to read a book set in medieval times, especially with a spunky heroine. But there were quite a few bawdy references, though they were made to be light or humourous. Perhaps it was like that back then, I don't know. I do know that I don't like that kind of humor, or that kind of talk in general. <br /><br />I certainly did not like the incessant taking of the name of deity in vain. I've never been all right hearing that in daily life, and I'm certainly not all right reading it in books. As I was listening to this book, it made it twice as hard for me to bear through it. <br /><br />I was also rather bored (and even disgusted) by the mentioning of each saints' day and why they were saints. Interesting, but still boring. Don't ask how, that's just the way it was for me. <br /><br />What I did like was the journal format. That the main character was spunky and did not want to conform to the role that everyone expected of her. That she grew quite a bit over the course of the book. How she learned to understand other people. How much she loved her mother. How loyal she was as a friend. And that she sought out and clung to hope so dearly. <br /><br />Perhaps I would have enjoyed and/or appreciated the book more if I'd read it when I was younger. I don't know. I'm not saying it's terrible, and that others shouldn't read it. It just wasn't for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4579347569508646980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81577402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81577402" />
    <a title="Lars Guthrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/757602-lars-guthrie"><img alt="Lars Guthrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199816668p2/757602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81577402?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lars Guthrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lars Guthrie" href="/user/show/757602-lars-guthrie">Lars Guthrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780064405843" href="/book/show/831951.Catherine_Called_Birdy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81577402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1056542075218823408">I'm foregoing a real review, except to say that I highly recommend this provocative and personal glimpse into the middle ages. Karen Cushman has done her research and put together a marvelous novel which should be an exciting find for young readers. Catherine is an exciting, witty and empathetic character whose 'journal' makes the work concrete and vibrant. <br/><br/>The problem, as I've noted with other great books such as 'Tuck Everlasting' and 'Dragonwings,' is that the joy of finding a good book that </span>
  <span id="freeText1056542075218823408" style="display:none">I'm foregoing a real review, except to say that I highly recommend this provocative and personal glimpse into the middle ages. Karen Cushman has done her research and put together a marvelous novel which should be an exciting find for young readers. Catherine is an exciting, witty and empathetic character whose 'journal' makes the work concrete and vibrant. <br /><br />The problem, as I've noted with other great books such as 'Tuck Everlasting' and 'Dragonwings,' is that the joy of finding a good book that truly fits you and inspires you has been robbed by 'Catherine, Called Birdy' being required reading, in this case for a seventh grader with whom I have been working. <br /><br />I don't think I'm reading too much into these types of requirements by assuming this they are assignments that have been recycled over many, many years. I know I've read this particular standard multiple, multiple times because kids with whom I work have to. They are assignments accompanied by 'guides' where wiley kids quickly surmise expected answers, while others miss them, but where answers are expected, and thus, right or wrong, and highly predictable. No real thinking is necessary.<br /><br />Is anyone energized by this kind of reading? Teachers or students? Not too often. It's a shame, especially when it's such a wonderful book that might open up new horizons if it could be discovered, instead of assigned. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1056542075218823408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2591840684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2591840684" />
    <a title="Chance Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2355889-chance-lee"><img alt="Chance Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551884443p2/2355889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2591840684?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chance Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chance Lee" href="/user/show/2355889-chance-lee">Chance Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780547722184" href="/book/show/13219040-catherine-called-birdy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2591840684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17671165006844784438">"I am left with a beastly father, a life of chores, no hope, no friends, no escape, and a large bosom!" writes Catherine in her journal on October 13, 1290. <br/><br/>Same. <br/><br/><i>Catherine, Called Birdy</i> is like <i>Bridget Jones's Diary</i> if Bridget were 14, adamantly uninterested in men, and living in the 13th century. Catherine (who is only called Birdy, like, twice), is a lady of a not un-wealthy knight, and she feels perpetually stuck. She wishes she were richer, rich enough to have servants do everything for her</span>
  <span id="freeText17671165006844784438" style="display:none">"I am left with a beastly father, a life of chores, no hope, no friends, no escape, and a large bosom!" writes Catherine in her journal on October 13, 1290. <br /><br />Same. <br /><br /><i>Catherine, Called Birdy</i> is like <i>Bridget Jones's Diary</i> if Bridget were 14, adamantly uninterested in men, and living in the 13th century. Catherine (who is only called Birdy, like, twice), is a lady of a not un-wealthy knight, and she feels perpetually stuck. She wishes she were richer, rich enough to have servants do everything for her, or poorer, poor enough to make her own decisions in love and marriage instead of being a piece of property for her father to barter with. As she journals her daily life, she muses on social class, gender differences, marriage, and religion. ("I wondered why Jesus used his miraculous powers to cure lepers instead of creating an herb or flower that would cure them so we could continue to use it even now when Jesus is in Heaven.")<br /><br />Like Bridget, who cataloged her calorie intake, cigarettes smoked, and alcohol units consumed everyday, Catherine tells us which saint's day every day is, after she comes into possession of a book of saints. The book catalogs mid-September 1290 to end of September 1291. Catherine finds the saints' book in October, and something terrible happens on September 7 (my birthday) making it the ONLY day she doesn't tell us which saint's day it is!!<br /><br />There is some beautiful writing in here, both humorous ("One day [my father's] angry liver will set him afire and I will toast bread on him") and touching ("When I was little, I used to try to capture the colored light. I thought I could hold it in my hand and carry it home. Now I know it is like happiness--it is there or it is not, you cannot hold it or keep it.")<br /><br />The most popular review of this book on here criticizes it for being "anachronistic" and having a "spunky, modern heroine," with no justification given for this interpretation, leaving me to assume it's because the main character is a young woman who questions her situation. That critique has me thinking of Mackenzi Lee, author of <i>The Gentleman's Guide to Vice and Virtue</i>, who said this criticism is often leveled at her own work, mostly by men who seem to find it unthinkable that there might have been ANY non-male (or non-white, or non-hetero) people in history who questioned their own culture. She said one reviewer -- an old, white, male historian -- said he finds it much more interesting for historical fiction to portray a power<i>less</i> woman instead of a powerful one. The review I mentioned of this book actually says, "I wish Cushman had created a protagonist who was both engaging to the reader and able to provide illumination of how much people have changed over time." <br /><br />That's exactly what Cushman does. <i>Catherine, Called Birdy</i> is an engaging work of historical fiction that shows both the similarities and differences between our times and Medieval ones. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17671165006844784438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_290268482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7182428-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329924427p2/7182428.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290268482?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/7182428-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7182428-emily?shelf=children-s-chapter">children-s-chapter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7182428-emily?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7182428-emily?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290268482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer534048461276468022">	Catherine, Called Birdy by Karen Cushman was not one of my favorite books. <br/>	Catherine had many of the characteristics of Ella from Ella Enchanted, such as determination, wit, and assertiveness, but without the vivacity which came through in the characterization of Ella. I found myself not really caring what happened to Catherine.<br/>	The format of the novel was interesting. Over the years, I’ve realized that writing in first person without becoming repetitive, pedantic and downright boring is diffi</span>
  <span id="freeText534048461276468022" style="display:none">	Catherine, Called Birdy by Karen Cushman was not one of my favorite books. <br />	Catherine had many of the characteristics of Ella from Ella Enchanted, such as determination, wit, and assertiveness, but without the vivacity which came through in the characterization of Ella. I found myself not really caring what happened to Catherine.<br />	The format of the novel was interesting. Over the years, I’ve realized that writing in first person without becoming repetitive, pedantic and downright boring is difficult. I like novels in the form of diaries, but this one just didn’t capture my attention. This book, if the information is accurate, would be an appropriate option for extra reading in a history or social studies course. Some if the information and customs written about through Catherine I did find interesting.<br />	The one redeeming part of this novel was the lesson which Catherine got from the Jewish woman. “I am who I am wherever I am,” comments Birdy toward the end of the novel. The lesson was good, and very appropriate for the young adult audience. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="534048461276468022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1718948965" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1718948965" />
    <a title="MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7428258-mj"><img alt="MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326573171p2/7428258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1718948965?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MJ" href="/user/show/7428258-mj">MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780547350103" href="/book/show/8578631-catherine-called-birdy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7428258-mj?shelf=recommendations">recommendations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7428258-mj?shelf=2016-summer">2016-summer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1718948965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16655303525878473296">I have memories of seeing this book on the shelf of my grade-school library, but for some reason I never got around to actually reading it. Now thanks to the magic of rentable ebooks, I can finally give myself the childhood reading experience I was lacking!!!<br/><br/>Or kind of. I think for sure that I would've loved this a lot more as a kid, yet at the same time I would've understood far less (all the references to people "tumbling" lmao). There's a real transitional feeling about this book; it's a perf</span>
  <span id="freeText16655303525878473296" style="display:none">I have memories of seeing this book on the shelf of my grade-school library, but for some reason I never got around to actually reading it. Now thanks to the magic of rentable ebooks, I can finally give myself the childhood reading experience I was lacking!!!<br /><br />Or kind of. I think for sure that I would've loved this a lot more as a kid, yet at the same time I would've understood far less (all the references to people "tumbling" lmao). There's a real transitional feeling about this book; it's a perfect picture of a girl going through teendom and all the moodswings that go with it, yet at the same time it's very much about a girl realizing that womanhood is upon her and has been upon her much longer than she thought. I went through (and still am going through) a lot of indecision over how much I liked the ending. It was abrupt, yes, but so were many things in Birdy's life. People were born and people died and barns burned and animals froze and you had to roll with the punches. Her marriage fate changing through nothing but an act of god was believable, yet somehow I still felt myself thinking "really?? that's IT???"<br /><br />As for Birdy herself, I loved her, surprising no one. I LOVED her. If I'd had a diary-esque book like this for a model as a kid I think I would've been a lot better at keeping a diary. She skipped days, she wrote down stupid questions and brainstorms she had, she was too tired or too cold or too busy to write more than one line on some days. She wondered about the world and the people she knew and took out her frustrations and aired her grievances and hoped for the future. My favorite passage in the whole book was the entry where she wrote about nothing but helping an ant get to the other side of road: "I felt like I had saved the whole world." I literally almost cried reading that. <br /><br />In the end, I decided to give this book 4 stars despite some of my misgivings, because ultimately I think it's one of the rare historical fiction books I've read that is relatable enough to modern readers yet still set in its own time enough to make you think harder about the psyche of the narrator and how it was shaped by her culture and history. I seriously wish I could rewind to age 14 and read it then. Corpus bones :')</span>
  <a data-text-id="16655303525878473296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8707105765694151173"><b>
  <u>2019</u>
</b><br/>2ND DAY OF MAY, <i>Feast of Saint Gennys, not the one who carried his own head</i><br/><br/><i> If I had to be born a lady, why not a <i>rich</i> lady, so someone else could do the work and I could lie on a silken bed and listen to a beautiful minstrel sing while my servants hemmed?</i><br/><br/>I have probably read through this book about 80 times since the first glorious time of reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24137.Catherine__Called_Birdy' title='Catherine, Called Birdy by Karen Cushman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Catherine, Called Birdy</a>.   <span id="freeText8707105765694151173" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>2019</u>
</b><br />2ND DAY OF MAY, <i>Feast of Saint Gennys, not the one who carried his own head</i><br /><br /><i> If I had to be born a lady, why not a <i>rich</i> lady, so someone else could do the work and I could lie on a silken bed and listen to a beautiful minstrel sing while my servants hemmed?</i><br /><br />I have probably read through this book about 80 times since the first glorious time of reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24137.Catherine__Called_Birdy" title="Catherine, Called Birdy by Karen Cushman" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine, Called Birdy</a>. I was only about 14 myself (same as the witty Catherine) when I first stumbled upon this book and, even though we are worlds apart based on the customs at the time, I felt a connection to Catherine that has continued even to today. Catherine was one of the first heroines that I related to on such a personal note. She was sarcastic, witty, charming (when she wanted to be), but she was definitely not a lady. She liked getting dirty and cursing (Corpus Bones!) and felt like she couldn't do anything right (especially not chores). Even today, rereading it when I am far from the age of 14, I can't help but fall right back into that mindset. This book truly is amazing no matter what age you are reading it at.<br /><br /><b>The cook's boy told me today of a miller's apprentice in Nottingham who can fart at will. That, I think, is a useful and notable talent.<br />...<br />So I set fire to the privy.<br />...<br />Luckily I am experienced at outwitting suitors.<br />...<br />Mayhap I could be a hermit. I wonder what they do.<br />...<br />Fought again with my father. God gave me this big mouth, so I think it can be no sin to use it.</b></span>

    <a title="Laura Garding" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4685197-laura-garding"><img alt="Laura Garding" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158810537?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Garding" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Garding" href="/user/show/4685197-laura-garding">Laura Garding</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780064405843" href="/book/show/831951.Catherine_Called_Birdy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158810537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14618579825049925163">There were a few times where I was a little bit bored with it. That could have been partly due to the fact that it was written for a much younger audience and some things I am just not interested in that I would have found fascinating when I was a teenager. It was a pretty fun book for the most part though. I was surprised at how much I laughed as I read this book. The main character was quite comical and had a very different personality than I was expecting. She acted very much like I would thi</span>
  <span id="freeText14618579825049925163" style="display:none">There were a few times where I was a little bit bored with it. That could have been partly due to the fact that it was written for a much younger audience and some things I am just not interested in that I would have found fascinating when I was a teenager. It was a pretty fun book for the most part though. I was surprised at how much I laughed as I read this book. The main character was quite comical and had a very different personality than I was expecting. She acted very much like I would think a young adult would. She seemed to complain nonstop and was very immature. I think that there are many young adults that could relate to Catherine in the book with the problems she has with her parents and also to all of the stress and drama she creates and has in her life.<br />I’m not sure that I would go out of my way to recommend this book to anyone. If someone asked me about it I would give them good feedback. It was a pleasant book to read with interesting things going on. I felt like the story line was lacking a little bit though. It just kind of started and not much happened to the story throughout the book. I felt like it didn’t have a super strong ending. It could have kept going and told more about her life and her getting married but it just kind of ended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14618579825049925163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_158569628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158569628" />
    <a title="Devon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4991178-devon"><img alt="Devon" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158569628?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Devon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Devon" href="/user/show/4991178-devon">Devon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158569628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3936671548825034637">Catherine Called Birdy was a witty, charming book to read. Catherine is such a great character because while she is aware that Edward will eventually read her journal, she is hilariously honest in her evaluations of people. She avoids her suitors at all costs, and comes up with all kinds of schemes to drive them away. Catherine is a relatable, down to earth character that feels real, with her devious nature and aversion to growing up, because while most teenagers want to be older and have more c</span>
  <span id="freeText3936671548825034637" style="display:none">Catherine Called Birdy was a witty, charming book to read. Catherine is such a great character because while she is aware that Edward will eventually read her journal, she is hilariously honest in her evaluations of people. She avoids her suitors at all costs, and comes up with all kinds of schemes to drive them away. Catherine is a relatable, down to earth character that feels real, with her devious nature and aversion to growing up, because while most teenagers want to be older and have more control of their lives, they fight against the responsibilities and chores that accompany growing up. The author is able to creatively tell a story through the use of Catherine’s diary entries and able to keep the reader fully engaged throughout the entire book. While there is not really a plot and the entries are scattered, it is a very accurate opinion of many girls' journals, which is one of the reasons the book is so much fun. This book could very accurately be labeled as a "girl book," but it is quirky and interesting enough that boys would find it amusing as well. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3936671548825034637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6826462233050703626"><br/> This book was a very fun read. I'm always a sucker for diary style fiction and this one was done especially well. Cushman really did her research about the time period and that's essential. I think this book wouldn't have been so effective if Birdy had modern ideals and attitudes. <br/><br/> I remember reading a book in high school that was supposed to be set during the Industrial Revolution but the main character acted as though she was living in modern times.   <span id="freeText6826462233050703626" style="display:none"><br /> This book was a very fun read. I'm always a sucker for diary style fiction and this one was done especially well. Cushman really did her research about the time period and that's essential. I think this book wouldn't have been so effective if Birdy had modern ideals and attitudes. <br /><br /> I remember reading a book in high school that was supposed to be set during the Industrial Revolution but the main character acted as though she was living in modern times. She traveled where she wanted, did what she wanted and talked about birth control so much I suspected that the book was put out by planned parenthood. In the end I couldn't connect with the book because I was too busy getting frustrated with the author's historical bloopers.<br /><br /> Birdy, on the other hand, is a pure delight and leaves you with the texture of that time period in England. This book is a jewel!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63291011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11135323109037475036">It's a little surprising that a Newberry Honor book like this has some pretty adult themes (aren't Newberries supposed to be juvenile fiction?). Comments like "since Meg the milk maid and Gerd the miller's son were found together in the barn, it looks like we'll need someone else to play the Virgin Mary in the Christmas play" (I am heavily paraphrasing, but that's the gist). Much mention of pissing and farting too. I suppose the author has given a realistic view of medieval life in all its gritt</span>
  <span id="freeText11135323109037475036" style="display:none">It's a little surprising that a Newberry Honor book like this has some pretty adult themes (aren't Newberries supposed to be juvenile fiction?). Comments like "since Meg the milk maid and Gerd the miller's son were found together in the barn, it looks like we'll need someone else to play the Virgin Mary in the Christmas play" (I am heavily paraphrasing, but that's the gist). Much mention of pissing and farting too. I suppose the author has given a realistic view of medieval life in all its gritty-ness, but I don't think I'd want my kids to read it until they are teens. Too bad, too, because it's pretty readable and the main character is funny and likeable. Very interesting, too, to read about all the Saint's Days that were celebrated (the book is in diary style). </span>

<div id="review_961785071" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/961785071" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2988548-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405106952p2/2988548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/961785071?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2988548-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2988548-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2988548-rebecca?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2988548-rebecca?shelf=lyrically-lovely">lyrically-lovely</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer961785071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7196131486989623338">Absolutely excellent. Best YA historical novel I've ever read. Thirteen year old Catherine records the doings at her father's manor's house the year before she gets married. Sassy and smart, Catherine would fit in perfectly in modern times, but she lives in a medieval world where women are supposed to know their place (under the heels of men). <br/><br/>But still, Catherine finds a way to make her mark on the world. <br/><br/>Highly recommended. This book deserved to win the Newberry award.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1799115823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1799115823" />
    <a title="Leah H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59698364-leah-h"><img alt="Leah H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477442059p2/59698364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1799115823?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah H." href="/user/show/59698364-leah-h">Leah H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1799115823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14661392749423381168">Catherine, Called Birdy is a book that I probably would't have picked up on my own, seeing as I am not a big fan of historical fiction books. The book wasn't like I expected it to be, and could be pretty interesting in some parts. I found it a bit slow in some parts, and the setup of the book was different then I was used to. It definitely wasn't a favorite of mine, but I would recommend it to anyone who really enjoys historical fiction books. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608866673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14074893014493045752">I found this book to be interesting at first, but then as it went on began to see how boring it actually was.. It was a new kind of writing style for me, that I have decided that I don't particularly enjoy. I would not recommend this book unless you like a diary style writing format </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lhl5CWGUBnl818xD3fDl38R3P23wuMrN+uPqn1rvG0106H2HkCXiQbC9R5sCrxoiTZMryKiezAdvQ6Y7eROTFw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rjiMWycXM0Y9/34ZW7LkPasbaVsvzV/sGFe+/xhHrl1MyYjV1qbXfvGV9cGE7RvAIv99/nfrWSaN9/JbO7smBw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer13794135351670419192">Karen Cushman was born in Chicago, Illinois. <br/><br/>She entered Stanford University on a scholarship in 1959 and graduated with degrees in Greek and English. She later earned master’s degrees in human behavior and museum studies.<br/><br/>For eleven years she was an adjunct professor in the Museum Studies Department at John F. Kennedy University before resigning in 1996 to write full-time. <br/><br/>She lives on Vashon Isla</span>
  <span id="freeText13794135351670419192" style="display:none">Karen Cushman was born in Chicago, Illinois. <br /><br />She entered Stanford University on a scholarship in 1959 and graduated with degrees in Greek and English. She later earned master’s degrees in human behavior and museum studies.<br /><br />For eleven years she was an adjunct professor in the Museum Studies Department at John F. Kennedy University before resigning in 1996 to write full-time. <br /><br />She lives on Vashon Island, Washington with her husband, Philip.<br /><br />(source: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://karencushman.com/about/bio.html">http://karencushman.com/about/bio.html</a> &amp; <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.arnenixoncenter.org/finding_aids/anc0006.htm">http://www.arnenixoncenter.org/findin...</a>)</span>
